iv

[Tuberculosis is as old as humanity itself. It has](https://ghoapi.azureedge.net/api/NCD_GLUC_04)

afflicted kings and queens, poets and politicians,

revolutionaries and writers, activists and actors.

[Dr Tedros Adhanom Ghebreyesus](http://www.wipo.int/amc/en/mediation/rules/) [Most of its victims, however, are poor, marginalised or](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/378535)

Director-General

malnourished, and the out-of-pocket costs associated

[World Health Organization](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/379015)

with treating TB expose them to financial hardship

or drive them further into poverty. TB is the definitive

disease of deprivation. Turning the tide on TB means

[screening and treatment for those it strikes, and](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/political-declaration-of-the-un-general-assembly-high-level-meeting-on-the-fight-against-tuberculosis)

[preventing it by addressing its drivers and developing a](http://data.worldbank.org/indicator/SH.XPD.CHEX.PP.CD)

[new vaccine.](https://undocs.org/A/RES/78/5)

Only by working together can we turn the tide against

this ancient killer.

[WHO’s Global tuberculosis report for 2024](https://ghoapi.azureedge.net/api/NCD_GLUC_04)

reveals a sobering reality: TB has probably

returned to being the world’s leading infectious

[Dr Tereza Kasaeva](http://www.wipo.int/amc/en/mediation/rules/) [disease killer. We are confronted with a multitude of](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/378535)

Director

formidable challenges: funding shortfalls, catastrophic

[WHO Global Tuberculosis Programme](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/379015)

financial burdens for many TB-affected households,

climate change, conflict, migration and displacement,

[pandemics, and the urgent need to tackle drug-resistant](https://ghoapi.azureedge.net/api/FINPROTECTION_CATA_TOT_10_POP)

[tuberculosis, a significant driver of antimicrobial](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/political-declaration-of-the-un-general-assembly-high-level-meeting-on-the-fight-against-tuberculosis)

resistance. It is imperative that we unite across all

sectors and stakeholders, to confront these pressing

issues and ramp up our efforts, transforming our

promises into tangible resources and unwavering

resolve. Only through our collective determination can

we make significant strides in our battle to end TB once

and for all.

v

## PRINCIPLES

| 1.  | Government stewardship and accountability, with monitoring and evaluation          |
| --- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| 2.  | Strong coalition with civil society organizations and communities                  |
| 3.  | Protection and promotion of human rights, ethics and equity                        |
| 4.  | Adaptation of the strategy and targets at country level, with global collaboration |

## [PILLARS AND COMPONENTS](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/political-declaration-of-the-un-general-assembly-high-level-meeting-on-the-fight-against-tuberculosis)

## 1. INTEGRATED, PATIENT-CENTRED CARE AND PREVENTION

A. Early diagnosis of TB including universal drug-susceptibility testing, and systematic screening of contacts and high-risk groups B. Treatment of all people with TB including drug-resistant TB, and patient support C. Collaborative TB/HIV activities, and management of comorbidities D. Preventive treatment of persons at high risk, and vaccination against TB

## 2. BOLD POLICIES AND SUPPORTIVE SYSTEMS

E. [Political commitment with adequate resources for TB care and prevention](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/345527) F. Engagement of communities, civil society organizations, and public and private care providers G. [Universal health coverage policy, and regulatory frameworks for case notification, vital registration, quality and](https://doi.org/10.1016/S1473-3099(18)30134-8) [rational use of medicines, and infection control](https://www.stoptb.org/global-plan-to-end-tb/global-plan-to-end-tb-2023-2030) H. [Social protection, poverty alleviation and actions on other determinants of TB](https://apps.who.int/iris/handle/10665/331934)

a

This indicator is for the combined total of TB deaths in HIV-negative and HIV-positive people. Deaths from TB among people with HIV are officially classified as deaths caused by HIV/AIDS, with TB as a contributory cause.

b

This indicator is not the same as the SDG indicator for catastrophic health expenditures. See Box 3 for further explanation.

## TABLE 2

[Highlights of commitments and requests at the second UN high-level meeting on TB in 2023](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/who-htm-tb-2015-29)

### a) Commitments

## [TOPIC OR THEME](https://hq_globaltuberculosisprogramme.createsend1.com/t/d-l-eviig-ihkktihjjl-t/) [COMMITMENT](https://hq_globaltuberculosisprogramme.createsend1.com/t/d-l-eviig-ihkktihjjl-t/)

[Strengthen the provision of comprehensive care for all people with TB, with particular attention to people](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/365308) who are vulnerable or in vulnerable situations (e.g. people with HIV, people with TB-associated disabilities, older people, migrants, refugees, internally displaced people, and pregnant and lactating women), using Provide comprehensive [specific models of care such as nutritional, mental health and psychosocial support, social protection,](http://bricstb.samrc.ac.za/) care to all people with TB rehabilitation and palliative care

Scale-up comprehensive efforts to close longstanding gaps in the prevention, diagnosis, treatment and care of children

Work towards the achievement of universal, equitable and affordable access to WHO-recommended [Address the crisis of drug-](https://www.who.int/data/gho/data/indicators/indicator-details/GHO/bcg-immunization-coverage-among-1-year-olds-(-) [diagnostics and drug susceptibility tests, and all-oral shorter-duration treatment regimens for people with](https://www.who.int/data/gho/data/indicators/indicator-details/GHO/bcg-immunization-coverage-among-1-year-olds-(-) resistant TB drug-resistant TB, complemented by monitoring and management of side-effects, together with care and support to improve treatment outcomes

Establish TB services as essential elements of national and global strategies to advance UHC, address Build on interlinkages antimicrobial resistance and strengthen PPPR across the global health agendas of TB, UHC and [Integrate systematic screening, prevention, treatment and care of TB, and related health conditions, within](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/259817) PPPR, to strengthen the primary health care, including community-based health services TB response [Invest in public health infrastructure and the health workforce](http://www.wipo.int/amc/en/mediation/rules/)

Address TB during health and humanitarian Safeguard TB services as essential health services during humanitarian and health emergencies emergencies

Intensify national efforts to create enabling legal and social policy frameworks to combat inequalities, and [Strengthen the](https://extranet.who.int/tbknowledge) [to eliminate all forms of TB-related stigma, discrimination and other human rights barriers and violations](https://www.who.int/publications/book-orders) engagement of civil Strengthen the meaningful engagement of parliaments, civil society, and TB-affected local communities, society and communities including young people and women, in all aspects of the TB response, to ensure equitable and peopleaffected by TB centred access to TB services, with increased and sustained investments, especially in community [initiatives](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/366277)

Create an enabling environment for TB research and innovation across Member States and partners

Strengthen research capacity and collaboration through TB research platforms and networks across the Enable and strengthen TB public and private sectors, academia and civil society research Accelerate the research, development and roll-out of safe, effective, affordable and accessible vaccines, preferably within the next 5 years, including through leveraging global collaboration mechanisms and WHO initiatives such as the accelerator council for new TB vaccines

Promote equitable access to affordable, safe, effective and quality medicines, such as generics, vaccines, Promote access to diagnostics and health technologies, including through the Stop TB Partnership/Global Drug Facility, to affordable medicines ensure availability and access to quality-assured and affordable commodities recommended by WHO

Support the WHO multisectoral accountability framework for TB by strengthening high-level multisectoral accountability and review mechanisms, in line with national contexts, defining the roles and responsibilities Strengthen multisectoral of relevant sectors and stakeholders with the meaningful engagement of people and communities affected accountability by TB

[Develop and implement ambitious, costed national TB strategic plans or health strategies with a](https://doi.org/10.1016/S1473-3099(18)30134-8) [multisectoral approach](https://www.stoptb.org/global-plan-to-end-tb/global-plan-to-end-tb-2023-2030)

### b) Requests

## TOPIC OR THEME REQUEST

WHO is requested to continue providing global leadership to support Member States to build a resilient [response to TB as an integral part of the UHC agenda, and to also address the drivers and determinants](https://www.who.int/publications/i/item/9789240083851) Role of WHO [of the epidemic, including in the context of health and humanitarian emergencies, with multisectoral](https://www.who.int/publications/i/item/9789240083851) [engagement, the provision of normative guidance and technical support, and through monitoring,](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/373901) [reporting and review of progress, and by advancing the TB research and innovation agenda](https://aidsinfo.unaids.org/)

[The UN Secretary-General, with the support of WHO, is requested to report, as part of his annual SDG](https://www.unaids.org/en/resources/documents/2024/global-aids-update-2024) report, on the global effort to end TB

The UN Secretary-General, with the support of WHO, is requested to present a report to the UN General Report and review [Assembly in 2027, on the progress achieved towards realizing the commitments made in the 2023 political](https://apps.who.int/gb/ebwha/pdf_files/WHA73/A73_R3-en.pdf) progress [declaration on TB](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376612)

Heads of state and government are requested to undertake a comprehensive review of progress at a UN [high-level meeting on TB in 2028](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/353829)

HIV: human immunodeficiency virus; PPPR: pandemic preparedness, prevention and response; SDG: Sustainable Development Goal; UHC: universal health coverage; UN: United Nations; WHO: World Health Organization.

### Number of people developing drug-resistant TB Burden stable or falling slowly

[Drug-resistant TB continues to be a public health threat.](https://www.stoptb.org/global-plan-to-end-tb/global-plan-to-end-tb-2023-2030) Resistance to rifampicin – the most effective first-line Thousands per year

drug – is of greatest concern. TB that is resistant to [rifampicin and isoniazid is defined as multidrug-resist-](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/who-multisectoral-accountability-framework-for-tb-(maf-tb)-baseline-assessment-checklist-for-country-use-in-pursuing-a-national-maf-tb) [ant TB (MDR-TB). Both MDR-TB and rifampicin-resistant](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/341072) TB (RR-TB) require treatment with second-line drugs. Globally, the estimated annual number [of](https://aidsinfo.unaids.org/) [peo-](https://aidsinfo.unaids.org/) oping TB were offset by an estimated downward trend ple who developed MDR-TB or RR-TB (MDR/RR-TB) [(since 2015) in the proportion of people with TB who](https://www.unaids.org/en/resources/documents/2024/global-aids-update-2024) was relatively flat between 2020 and 2023 ( [Fig. 6](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/365806) [),](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/365806) [have MDR/RR-TB, particularly among those with a pre-](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376221) after a slow downward trend between 2015 and 2020. vious history of treatment ( Fig. 7 ). People with no previous history of TB treatment

### Deaths caused by TB [Continued global fall in 2023 after COVID-related](https://sdgs.un.org/) [increases](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/378536)

[The estimated global number of deaths caused by TB](http://apps.who.int/gb/ebwha/pdf_files/WHA67/A67_R1-en.pdf) [fell for a second consecutive year in 2023, continuing](https://ghoapi.azureedge.net/api/MDG_0000000029)

Perentage [the reversal of increases that occurred during the worst](https://ghoapi.azureedge.net/api/MDG_0000000029) [period of COVID-related disruptions to TB diagnosis and](https://ghoapi.azureedge.net/api/NCD_GLUC_04) treatment in 2020 and 2021 ( Fig. 9 ). Globally in 2023, TB caused an estimated 1.25 million [deaths (95% UI: 1.13–1.37 million), including 1.09 million](https://ghoapi.azureedge.net/api/SA_0000001462) among HIV-negative people (95% UI: 0.98–1.20 million)

[People previously treated for TB](http://www.wipo.int/amc/en/mediation/rules/)

[and 161 000 among people with HIV (95% UI: 132 000–](https://ghoapi.azureedge.net/api/M_Est_smk_curr_std) 193 000). [This total was down from estimates of 1.32](https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/igo/) million (95% UI: 1.21–1.45 million) in 2022, 1.42 million [(95% UI: 1.29–1.55 million) in 2021 and 1.40 million](https://www.who.int/publications/book-orders) (95% UI: 1.27–1.54 million) in 2020; it was also below the pre-pandemic level of 1.34 million (95% UI: 1.22–1.46

Percentage million) in 2019. [COVID-related disruptions are estimated to have](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/political-declaration-of-the-un-general-assembly-high-level-meeting-on-the-fight-against-tuberculosis) resulted in almost 700 000 excess deaths from TB in the 4 years 2020–2023, compared with the number that would have occurred if pre-pandemic trends had been maintained ( [Fig. 10](https://www.who.int/tb/data/en/) [).](https://www.who.int/tb/data/en/) Global trends in the number of deaths caused by TB differ by HIV status ( [Fig. 9](http://data.worldbank.org/indicator/NY.GDP.PCAP.PP.KD) [,](http://data.worldbank.org/indicator/NY.GDP.PCAP.PP.KD) [Fig. 11](http://data.worldbank.org/indicator/NY.GDP.PCAP.PP.KD) [). Deaths from TB](http://data.worldbank.org/indicator/NY.GDP.PCAP.PP.KD) among HIV-negative people drove the overall trend, [with a rise in 2020 and 2021 followed by falls in 2022](http://data.worldbank.org/indicator/SI.POV.GINI) and 2023, to just below the pre-pandemic level of 1.11 [million in 2019 (95% UI: 1.00–1.23 million).](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/373828) [Deaths from](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/373828) [TB among people with HIV have been falling steadily for](https://unstats.un.org/SDGAPI/v1/sdg/Series/Data?seriesCode=EN_LND_SLUM) [many years.](https://www.stoptb.org/global-plan-to-end-tb/global-plan-to-end-tb-2023-2030) In 2023, TB probably returned to being the world’s leading cause of death from a single infectious agent, [following 3 years in which it was replaced by COVID-19](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/363752)

Further details are provided in the report webpages (section 1.3). People with TB who remain undiagnosed and untreated have a [higher risk of death than those started on treatment. Disruptions](https://www.unaids.org/en/resources/documents/2024/global-aids-update-2024) [to TB diagnosis and treatment have a more immediate impact](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376221) on TB mortality and a more delayed impact on TB incidence. Similarly, recoveries in access to TB diagnosis and treatment have [a more immediate effect on TB mortality and a more delayed](https://apps.who.int/gb/ebwha/pdf_files/WHA73/A73_R3-en.pdf) impact on TB incidence. [Deaths from TB among people with HIV are officially classified](https://www.treatmentactiongroup.org/resources/tbrd-report/tbrd-report-2023/) [as deaths from HIV/AIDS. Therefore, a clear distinction between](https://population.un.org/wpp/) deaths among HIV-negative people and those among people with [HIV is made in](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/352522) [Fig. 9](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/352522) [,](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/352522) [Fig. 11](https://www.who.int/news/item/05-06-2023-who-launches-the-tb-research-tracker--an-online-platform-to-track-progress-in-tb-research) [and](https://www.who.int/news/item/05-06-2023-who-launches-the-tb-research-tracker--an-online-platform-to-track-progress-in-tb-research) [Fig. 12](https://www.who.int/news/item/05-06-2023-who-launches-the-tb-research-tracker--an-online-platform-to-track-progress-in-tb-research) [.](https://www.who.int/news/item/05-06-2023-who-launches-the-tb-research-tracker--an-online-platform-to-track-progress-in-tb-research) The estimate is a cumulative total of 676 648 in these 4 years. The estimated number of deaths caused by TB among HIV- negative people was 1.16 million (95% UI: 1.03–1.29 million) in 2020 and 1.20 million (95% UI: 1.08–1.33 million) in 2021.

[fications before, during and in the aftermath of the](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/378472) COVID-19 pandemic vary ( Fig. 17 ). The pattern in the WHO South-East Asia Region is very [similar to the global trend, with a big reduction (of 24%)](https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/igo) between 2019 and 2020 followed by a partial recovery in 2021 and then a strong rebound to above the pre-COVID level in 2022–2023; indeed, it is this region that drove the [trend at global level. There were similar patterns in the](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376584) Millions per year

WHO Eastern Mediterranean Region (mostly influenced by trends in Pakistan) and the Region of the Americas. In the WHO European Region, notifications fell at a [rate above the historic trend in 2020, increased in 2021](http://www.wipo.int/amc/en/mediation/rules/) (probably representing some backlog from 2020) and [then returned to a downward trend in 2022–2023.](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/379015) In the WHO Western Pacific Region, case notifica- [tions in 2023 recovered to the 2019 level, following a big](https://extranet.who.int/tbknowledge) drop in 2020–2021. The recovery in 2023 in the Western Pacific Region was driven by China and the Philippines,

TB treatment coverage in](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/353829) the European Region in 2023 is underestimated, because at the time the data snapshot for this report was taken (29 July 2024), 15 countries had not yet reported notification data for 2023 to WHO ( Annex 2 [). Once data from these countries have been reported, it is anticipated that treatment coverage in](https://www.who.int/news/item/05-06-2023-who-launches-the-tb-research-tracker--an-online-platform-to-track-progress-in-tb-research) 2023 will be similar to the level of 2022.

### Global coverage of preventive treatment improving

The main health care intervention available to reduce FIG. 28 the risk of TB infection progressing to active TB disease [is TB preventive treatment. Other preventive inter-](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/379015) Global coverage of TB preventive treatment, ventions are TB infection prevention and control, and [2015–2023](https://www.who.int/publications/book-orders) [vaccination of children with the bacille Calmette-Guérin](https://extranet.who.int/tbknowledge) (BCG) vaccine, which can confer protection, especially

Target for 2027 set at the 2023 UN high-level meeting on TB

from severe forms of TB in children. WHO recommends TB preventive [treatment](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/political-declaration-of-the-un-general-assembly-high-level-meeting-on-the-fight-against-tuberculosis) [for](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/political-declaration-of-the-un-general-assembly-high-level-meeting-on-the-fight-against-tuberculosis) [people living with HIV, household contacts of people](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/political-declaration-of-the-un-general-assembly-high-level-meeting-on-the-fight-against-tuberculosis) diagnosed with bacteriologically confirmed pulmonary TB and clinical risk groups (e.g. those receiving dialysis) (29) . Options include a weekly dose of isoniazid and rifapentine for 3 months, a daily dose of isoniazid and

UHC service coverage index (SDG 3.8.1)

a

The SCI can take values from 0 (worst) to 100 (best) and is calculated using 16 tracer indicators, one of which is the coverage of TB treatment. Values shown for the SCI are estimates for the latest year for which data for SDG 3.8.2 are available. Values are based on interpolated points between available years over the 2000-2021 period.

b

Defined as ≥10% of total household consumption or income. The latest available year ranges from 2007 to 2021 for the 30 high TB burden countries.

## 3. Main findings and messages

[Box 3. The difference between “catastrophic total costs” for TB-affected households,](https://www.who.int/initiatives/tuberculosis-vaccine-accelerator-council) [and the SDG UHC indicator related to household expenditures on health care](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/who-htm-tb-2015-29)

It is important to distinguish between SDG Indicator used as a measure of financial barriers to access to health [3.8.2, “the proportion of the population with large](https://hq_globaltuberculosisprogramme.createsend1.com/t/d-l-eviig-ihkktihjjl-t/) [care.](https://hq_globaltuberculosisprogramme.createsend1.com/t/d-l-eviig-ihkktihjjl-t/) household expenditures on health as a share of total [Due to the nature of the illness, people with TB and their](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/365308) household expenditure or income”, and “the percentage [households can face severe direct and indirect financial](http://data.worldbank.org/indicator/per_allsp.cov_pop_tot) [of TB-affected households facing catastrophic total costs](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376548) [and economic costs. These pose barriers that can greatly](http://data.worldbank.org/indicator/per_allsp.cov_pop_tot) [due to TB”, which is an indicator within the WHO End TB](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/378472) [affect their ability to access diagnosis and treatment, and](https://sdgs.un.org/) Strategy. to complete treatment successfully. Costs included in The SDG indicator is for the general population [.](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/378536) [the TB-specific indicator include not only](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/378536) direct medical [Household expenditures on health are defined as](https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/igo) [direct](https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/igo) [payments](http://apps.who.int/gb/ebwha/pdf_files/WHA67/A67_R1-en.pdf) [for diagnosis and treatment, but also](http://apps.who.int/gb/ebwha/pdf_files/WHA67/A67_R1-en.pdf) [direct](https://www.who.int/data/gho/data/indicators/indicator-details/GHO/bcg-immunization-coverage-among-1-year-olds-(-) [expenditures](https://www.who.int/data/gho/data/indicators/indicator-details/GHO/bcg-immunization-coverage-among-1-year-olds-(-) [on health by all household members who](https://www.who.int/data/gho/data/indicators/indicator-details/GHO/bcg-immunization-coverage-among-1-year-olds-(-) [nonmedical payments](https://www.who.int/data/gho/data/indicators/indicator-details/GHO/bcg-immunization-coverage-among-1-year-olds-(-) [(e.g. for transport and lodging)](https://ghoapi.azureedge.net/api/MDG_0000000029) seek any type of care (preventive, curative, rehabilitative [and indirect costs (e.g. lost income). ## 3. Main findings and messages

## TABLE 4

[WHO initiatives in TB research and innovation, 2023–2024 (ordered by month and year)](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/who-htm-tb-2015-29)

## RELEVANT COMMITMENTS TIMING ACTIVITY AT THE 2023 UN HIGH-LEVEL [MEETING ON TB](https://unstats.un.org/SDGAPI/v1/sdg/Series/Data?seriesCode=SI_POV_DAY1) [(9)](https://unstats.un.org/SDGAPI/v1/sdg/Series/Data?seriesCode=SI_POV_DAY1)

September TB trial platform Articles 67, 72, 73 and 74 WHO convened a consultation on establishing a “trial platform” to fast track the testing and [evaluation of promising regimens for treating TB. This initiative will establish a master protocol](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376548) [to evaluate multiple treatment regimens simultaneously, including through adaptive platform](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/378472) [designs. The aim of this approach is to improve trial efficiency (compared with traditional](http://bricstb.samrc.ac.za/) methods) and foster collaboration among countries, clinical trial sponsors, funders and civil society.

May 2024 [TB vaccine accelerator council](https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/igo) [Article 76](http://apps.who.int/gb/ebwha/pdf_files/WHA67/A67_R1-en.pdf) WHO hosted the second meeting of the TB vaccine accelerator council (49) . [Since the launch of the council in September 2023, WHO has convened a series of meetings](https://www.who.int/data/gho/data/indicators/indicator-details/GHO/bcg-immunization-coverage-among-1-year-olds-(-) to gather insights about the council’s work on accelerating the translation of scientific breakthroughs into effective and accessible TB vaccines. Following discussions between WHO [and council representatives, key goals and associated milestones for the council’s first term,](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376584) from 2024 to 2025, were agreed upon.

March 2024 [Investment case for TB screening and preventive treatment](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/259817) [Articles 39, 42, 45, 48, 49,](https://ghoapi.azureedge.net/api/SA_0000001462) [WHO released an investment case for TB screening and preventive treatment, aligned with the](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376549) 50, 53, 62, 65, 66, and 68 global target for coverage of TB preventive treatment agreed at the 2023 UN high-level meeting [on TB. The investment case was developed collaboratively with Brazil, Georgia, Kenya and](http://www.wipo.int/amc/en/mediation/rules/) [South Africa. It highlights that relatively modest investments could yield substantial health](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/378535) and economic benefits, offering a societal return of up to US$ 39 per dollar invested [(50)](https://ghoapi.azureedge.net/api/M_Est_smk_curr_std) .

March 2024 [TB sequencing portal](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/379015) Article 55 WHO launched a TB sequencing portal to share the most advanced knowledge base for sequencing and phenotyping Mycobacterium tuberculosis [. It was developed in collaboration](https://www.who.int/publications/book-orders) [with FIND and Unitaid. The portal features more than 56 000 sequences and visualizations of](https://www.who.int/copyright) the data used in the WHO mutation catalogue [(51)](https://www.who.int/copyright) [.](https://www.who.int/copyright)

February Consultation on the translation of TB research into global policy guidelines [Article 74](https://ghoapi.azureedge.net/api/FINPROTECTION_CATA_TOT_10_POP) WHO convened this annual consultation to exchange views on emerging areas of need for [global TB policy guidance, in the context of the existing landscape of evidence](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/political-declaration-of-the-un-general-assembly-high-level-meeting-on-the-fight-against-tuberculosis) [(52)](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/political-declaration-of-the-un-general-assembly-high-level-meeting-on-the-fight-against-tuberculosis) [.](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/political-declaration-of-the-un-general-assembly-high-level-meeting-on-the-fight-against-tuberculosis)

2023–2024 [BRICS TB research network](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/political-declaration-of-the-un-general-assembly-high-level-meeting-on-the-fight-against-tuberculosis) Article 73 WHO continues to engage with and support various research platforms and networks, including serving as the Secretariat of the BRICS TB research network to accelerate collective efforts towards ending TB [(53)](https://undocs.org/A/RES/78/5) [.](https://undocs.org/A/RES/78/5)

### Box 4. WHO recommendations related to TB prevention, diagnosis and treatment issued in 2024

Several new WHO recommendations related to TB prevention, diagnosis and treatment were issued in 2024.

[In March, recommendations on targeted next-generation sequencing were published as part of updated guidelines on](https://doi.org/10.1016/S1473-3099(18)30134-8) [TB diagnostics and an associated operational handbook](https://www.stoptb.org/global-plan-to-end-tb/global-plan-to-end-tb-2023-2030) [(20, 54)](https://www.stoptb.org/global-plan-to-end-tb/global-plan-to-end-tb-2023-2030) [.](https://www.stoptb.org/global-plan-to-end-tb/global-plan-to-end-tb-2023-2030)

In April, a recommendation for the co-administration of treatment for MDR/RR-TB and hepatitis C was released [(55)](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/346387) [.](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/346387)

In May, consolidated guidelines and an accompanying handbook on TB and comorbidities were published, which [include content about HIV and mental health](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/who-multisectoral-accountability-framework-for-tb-(maf-tb)-baseline-assessment-checklist-for-country-use-in-pursuing-a-national-maf-tb) [(56, 57)](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/who-multisectoral-accountability-framework-for-tb-(maf-tb)-baseline-assessment-checklist-for-country-use-in-pursuing-a-national-maf-tb) [.](https://www.who.int/publications/m/item/who-multisectoral-accountability-framework-for-tb-(maf-tb)-baseline-assessment-checklist-for-country-use-in-pursuing-a-national-maf-tb)

In August, updates to treatment recommendations for people with MDR/RR-TB were announced; these include a new 6-month regimen composed of bedaquiline, delamanid and linezolid, combined with levofloxacin or clofazimine [or both, as well as options for 9-month regimens for people with MDR/RR-TB who do not have resistance to](https://aidsinfo.unaids.org/) fluoroquinolones (28) .

[In September, updated guidelines on TB preventive treatment were published, including a new recommendation for](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376221) people exposed to MDR/RR-TB (29, 58) [. Updated recommendations for concurrent diagnostic testing for TB in adults](https://www.unaids.org/en/resources/documents/2024/global-aids-update-2024) and adolescents living with HIV and in children were also published (59) . These recommendations include use of the [LF-LAM assay in adults and adolescents living with HIV; molecular tests on respiratory specimens and stool in children;](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376612) and concurrent use of molecular tests on respiratory samples, stool and the LF-LAM assay on urine in children living with HIV.

New WHO guidelines and operational handbooks, as well as training modules and other documents to support the [production of evidence-based recommendations, can be found on the WHO TB Knowledge Sharing Platform](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/352522) [(60)](https://www.who.int/news/item/05-06-2023-who-launches-the-tb-research-tracker--an-online-platform-to-track-progress-in-tb-research) [.](https://www.who.int/news/item/05-06-2023-who-launches-the-tb-research-tracker--an-online-platform-to-track-progress-in-tb-research) [The platform was launched in 2021 and is continually updated with the latest resources in different languages. Pages](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/352522) in Arabic and Portuguese were first released in mid-2024. A search tool based on artificial intelligence will be made [available by the end of 2024.](https://www.unaids.org/en/resources/fact-sheet)

Global tuberculosis report 2024

## 4. [Conclusions](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376301)

## ANNEX 3

## [WHO global lists of high TB burden countries](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/275383)

A3.1 Background WHO conducted a consultation process in 2020 and

NA, not applicable; VR, vital registration

a

[Data for the period 2000–2009 can inform estimates for the period 2010–2023 and are shown for this reason. The 3 global TB watchlist countries are](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376221) Cambodia, the Russian Federation and Zimbabwe.

b

The WHO TB surveillance checklist of standards and benchmarks is designed to assess the quality and coverage of notification data, VR data and surveillance data related to drug-resistant TB, HIV co-infection and childhood TB. The second edition of the WHO TB surveillance checklist also includes an [assessment of surveillance related to TB care and TB prevention. If more than two assessments have been done, the years of the last two only are shown.](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376612)

c

[Studies are planned in Mongolia, the Philippines and Viet Nam for 2025. Prioritization of TB inventory studies is recommended in countries where a large](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/376612) share of TB care is provided to people with TB outside the existing NTP network.

d

[Brazil does not meet the following criteria recommended by the WHO Global Task Force on TB Impact Measurement for implementing a national](https://www.treatmentactiongroup.org/resources/tbrd-report/tbrd-report-2023/) [prevalence survey: TB incidence ≥150 per 100 000 population per year, no VR system and under-5 mortality rate (probability of dying by age of 5 per 1000](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/353829) live births) is >10.

e

Data points are shown for people without a history of previous TB treatment only. Data are available from continuous surveillance (indicated by italics [in blue cell) based on routine diagnostic testing in Angola, China, Ethiopia, India, Kenya, Lesotho, Mongolia, Mozambique, Myanmar, Namibia, Pakistan](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/352522) [(subnational only), the Philippines, South Africa, Uganda, the United Republic of Tanzania, Viet Nam, Zambia and Zimbabwe.](https://iris.who.int/handle/10665/352522)

f

[Years of data availability for Indonesia, Mongolia, Pakistan and South Africa were provided to WHO by IHME.](https://www.who.int/news/item/05-06-2023-who-launches-the-tb-research-tracker--an-online-platform-to-track-progress-in-tb-research)

g

Input data used to inform the covariates for estimating TB mortality in Cambodia available here: Ma, J., Vongpradith, A., Ledesma, J.R. et al. Progress towards the 2020 milestones of the end TB strategy in Cambodia: estimates of age and sex specific TB incidence and mortality from the Global Burden of Disease Study 2019. BMC Infect Dis 22, 904 (2022). [https://doi.org/10.1186/s12879-022-07891-5.](https://doi.org/10.1186/s12879-022-07891-5.)
